So it's 2025, I finally started watching OMITB, which led me to watching old Steve Martin, watched Father of the Bride and just found out right now that this exists. This was at the very beginning of the pandemic when people were dropping like flies. At first I thought that while this is a cute idea, I was surprised a movie known for being a depiction of an artificially perfect family that almost no one gets to have would be showcased in that moment, when so many families were suffering, losing loved ones, and never had that Banks family perfection to begin with. But these are some of the best actors around and the charm won me over. It says a lot about the acting quality when even a Zoom movie can get the job done. I think I read that the original din't get glowing reviews, but over the years, it has been watched by so many young brides who love their father just like this. I hope these so-called artificial movies continue to be made. It might be remarkable and rare to see a loving and happy family, but they exist, and bless us all.

I grew up watching Father of the Bride and Father of the Bride Part 2. They were both some of my absolute favorite movies. I always dreamed of having a wedding and a house like the ones in the movie. My husband and I were supposed to get married on 6/13/2020. In the end, that obviously didn't happen. But, like Matty, I decided that after 9 years together and in the middle of some of the scariest times we'd faced, I didn't want to wait any longer. We got married via Zoom in our living room while my parents watched outside the doorway so that we could be safe. We ate cake on our deck and had dinner delivered to our small studio apartment (a fraction of the size of the Banks' home). I've always felt a little sad when I've thought about not having the wedding (although next year we will be having a small vow renewal celebration). But watching this, two years late, I started to cry. Thank you so much for this beautiful short. To know that, in a strange twist of fate, I actually did get married Father of the Bride style brought me so much joy. Thank you for reminding me that it is the people and the love shared between them that makes the Banks family worth aspiring to, not simply where or how you celebrate it.

I dismissed FTOB as just another chick flick, until one night in 1993, when I came home from work after a really crappy day at work and this movie was one one of the subscription channels. I'd always liked Steve Martin and had been a fan of Diane Keaton since I saw her in "Sleeper," in the '70s. After watching the film while enjoying a couple of beers, I'd forgotten all about how bad the day had been. I saw the sequel with my girlfriend of the time, in early 1996, and it was good but didn't quite have the charm of the original. That said, both films are wonderfully cast and a perfect way to escape from the realities of life for a couple of hours. It's also great to see an Austin-Healey 3000 featured (I owned one for many years) in a film, although sharp-eyed watchers will note that a different Healey was used for FOTB2.
